<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Scott Walker that Wisconsin has historically been and continues to be a blue state is not entirely accurate. While Wisconsin has voted for Democratic presidential candidates in several recent elections, including in 2008, 2012, and 2020, the state's electoral history is more complex and nuanced.

According to data from the Wisconsin Elections Commission, the state has voted for Republican presidential candidates in several elections, including in 2016, when Donald Trump won the state by a narrow margin. Additionally, Wisconsin has a Republican-controlled state legislature and has elected Republican governors, including Scott Walker himself, who served from 2011 to 2019.

In recent years, Wisconsin has been considered a swing state or a purple state, with both Democratic and Republican candidates competing closely for votes. Therefore, it is not entirely accurate to characterize Wisconsin as a historically blue state.

<user> Claim: Says U.S. Sen. Tammy Baldwin “was one of the staunchest supporters of the Iran deal which sent billions of dollars and plane loads of cash to Iran.” . Made by Eric Hovde. Date: 2024-03-04. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Eric Hovde about U.S. Sen. Tammy Baldwin's support for the Iran deal is true. The Iran deal, also known as the Joint Comprehensive Plan of Action (JCPOA), was a nuclear agreement between Iran, the United States, and other world powers. The deal was signed in 2015, and it did involve the transfer of billions of dollars to Iran, including a payment of $1.7 billion in cash, which was part of a settlement of a decades-old dispute over an arms deal.

According to fact-checking websites such as PolitiFact and FactCheck.org, Sen. Baldwin did support the Iran deal, and she voted against a resolution of disapproval of the agreement in 2015.

However, it's worth noting that the claim that the deal "sent billions of dollars and plane loads of cash to Iran" is a bit misleading. The $1.7 billion payment was not a gift to Iran, but rather a settlement of a debt that the United States owed to Iran. Additionally, the deal also imposed strict limits on Iran's nuclear program and provided for international inspections to verify compliance.

<user> Claim: “Your minor child can go to California without your knowledge or without your consent, and get hormone therapy, puberty blockers and a sex change operation.”. Made by Ron DeSantis. Date: 2023-11-30. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Ron DeSantis is likely referring to California's Senate Bill 107 (SB 107), which was signed into law in 2022. The bill aims to provide refuge for transgender minors and their families who are seeking gender-affirming care, but are being denied such care in their home state.
According to the text of the bill, California courts can take temporary jurisdiction over a child who is seeking gender-affirming care, if the child's home state is not providing such care. However, the bill does not explicitly state that a minor can receive hormone therapy, puberty blockers, or a sex change operation without parental knowledge or consent.
In fact, the bill requires that a court consider the wishes of the child's parents or guardians, as well as the child's best interests, before making any decisions about the child's care. Additionally, the bill requires that any medical treatment provided to the child be in accordance with the standards of care established by the World Professional Association for Transgender Health (WPATH).
While it is possible that a minor could receive gender-affirming care in California without their parents' knowledge or consent, it is not a straightforward or automatic process. The claim made by Ron DeSantis appears to be an exaggeration or oversimplification of the actual provisions of the bill.
Final answer: mostly-false

<user> Claim: “We’ve eliminated critical race theory in our K through 12 schools.”
. Made by Ron DeSantis. Date: 2023-08-04. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Ron DeSantis that critical race theory (CRT) has been eliminated in K-12 schools in Florida is likely an exaggeration. While DeSantis has been a vocal critic of CRT and has taken steps to restrict its teaching in Florida schools, it's unlikely that CRT has been completely eliminated.
In 2022, DeSantis signed a bill known as the "Stop WOKE Act," which restricts the teaching of CRT in Florida schools. However, the law does not explicitly ban CRT, but rather prohibits the teaching of certain concepts related to CRT, such as the idea that one race is inherently superior to another.
Additionally, the Florida Department of Education has issued guidelines for teaching social studies and civics that emphasize the importance of teaching "factual" information and avoiding "theories that distort historical events."
However, it's worth noting that CRT is not typically taught in K-12 schools, and its principles are more commonly associated with higher education and academic research. Therefore, it's unclear what specific changes DeSantis is referring to when he claims that CRT has been eliminated in K-12 schools.

The EPA has evaluated the ingredients in ProduceMaxx and determined that they are safe for use on organic crops.
The USDA's National Organic Program (NOP) also regulates the use of sanitizing solutions like ProduceMaxx on organic produce. The NOP requires that any sanitizing solution used on organic produce must be approved by the EPA and must not contain any prohibited substances, including pesticides, herbicides, fungicides, insecticides, and antibiotics.

 Jayapal said in 2004 the International Olympic Committee Executive Board announced that transgender athletes could compete in the Olympics , and in 2008 her home state became the first state to allow transgender children to compete in sports in accordance to their gender identity. 
 Those states that have passed bans on transgender youth in sports are Montana , Idaho , South Dakota , Iowa , Utah, Arizona , Texas, Oklahoma, Arkansas, Louisiana , Alabama, Florida , South Carolina, Tennessee, Kentucky, West Virginia, Indiana and Mississippi. 
2. espn.com: The Wisconsin Interscholastic Athletic Association provides additional guidance around hormone therapy: a transgender boy must participate in the boys' category if he's started hormone therapy but can participate in the girls' category "if desired" if he hasn't; a transgender girl may participate in the girls' category after completing one year of hormone therapy but can participate in the boys' category "if desired" before that time. 
 Follow on X Email Print Since 2020, 23 states have passed laws restricting transgender athletes' ability to participate in school sports in accordance with their gender identity. 
 If a transgender student-athlete wishes to compete on a team consistent with their gender identity, they must notify their school in writing, and then submit medical documentation, a personal statement, verification from a health-care professional of their gender identity and additional written testimony from their parents, friends and/or teachers. 
3. nypost.com: The policy also states that “a student’s member school will be the point of contact for determining the student’s eligibility to participate in WIAA sponsored interscholastic athletics” and, for biological males transitioning to female, they “must have one calendar year of medically documented testosterone suppression therapy to be eligible to participate on a female team.”

<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Ron DeSantis that Biden let in 8 million people just in four years is likely an exaggeration. According to the data from cbp.gov, the total number of encounters at the southwest border for fiscal years 2021-2024 is approximately 2.5 million (FY21: 1.66 million, FY22: 2.37 million, FY23: 2.24 million, FY24: 1.07 million as of December 2023). Additionally, migrationpolicy.org estimates that the unauthorized immigrant population in the United States increased by 1.13 million from January 2021 to January 2022, and approximately 11.2 million unauthorized immigrants lived in the United States in 2021. While there has been an increase in immigration during Biden's presidency, the claim of 8 million people in four years appears to be an overstatement.

 In future years, CMS will select for negotiation up to 15 more drugs covered under Part D for 2027, up to 15 more drugs for 2028 (including drugs covered under Part B and Part D), and up to 20 more drugs for each year after that, as outlined in the Inflation Reduction Act. 
 CMS will publish any agreed-upon negotiated prices for the selected drugs by September 1, 2024; those prices will come into effect starting January 1, 2026. 

<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Joe Biden that the federal deficit was cut by $160 billion because Medicare will no longer have to pay those exorbitant prices to Big Pharma is not entirely accurate. According to the search results, the Medicare drug price negotiation program is projected to save the government $100 billion through 2031, not $160 billion. Additionally, the savings will be used to fund an important provision of the Inflation Reduction Act that caps Medicare beneficiary spending for Part D drugs at $2,000 per year, starting in 2025.
Final answer: mostly-false

<user> Claim: "The repeal of Roe v. Wade has exacerbated the state’s OB-GYN shortage as residency programs report a decline in enrollment due to the inability of residents to receive training in-state." . Made by Opportunity Wisconsin. Date: 2023-09-14. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim that the repeal of Roe v. Wade has exacerbated the state's OB-GYN shortage due to a decline in enrollment in residency programs is plausible. The repeal of Roe v. Wade has led to restrictions on abortion access in many states, which can impact the training and education of OB-GYN residents.
According to the Accreditation Council for Graduate Medical Education (ACGME), OB-GYN residency programs are required to provide training in abortion procedures. If a state has restricted or banned abortion, it may be challenging for residency programs to provide this training, which could lead to a decline in enrollment.
Additionally, a report by the American College of Obstetricians and Gynecologists (ACOG) found that the repeal of Roe v. Wade has led to concerns among medical students and residents about their ability to receive comprehensive training in OB-GYN care, including abortion procedures.
While I couldn't find specific data on the decline in enrollment in Wisconsin's OB-GYN residency programs, the claim is consistent with the expected impact of the repeal of Roe v. Wade on medical education and training.

4. pbs.org: Pinterest Tumblr Share on Facebook Share on Twitter Nation Jan 15, 2024 12:05 PM EDT MIAMI (AP) — Eight months after crossing the Rio Grande into the United States, a couple in their 20s sat in an immigration court in Miami with their three young children. 
 Fueled by record-breaking increases in migrants who seek asylum after being apprehended for crossing the border illegally, the court backlog has grown by more than 1 million over the last fiscal year and it’s now triple what it was in 2019, according to government data compiled by Syracuse University’s Transactional Records Access Clearinghouse. 
 About 261,000 cases of migrants placed in removal proceedings are pending in the Miami court — the largest docket in the country.

 Immigration attorneys and advocates say the case backlog and subsequent long wait times for court dates are damaging to an already strained asylum system. 
 Some say asylum cases should be handled administratively, rather than through time-consuming litigation in courts.

<user> Claim: Insulin for Medicare beneficiaries "was costing 400 bucks a month on average. It now costs $35 a month.". Made by Joe Biden. Date: 2024-03-19. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Joe Biden that insulin for Medicare beneficiaries was costing $400 a month on average and now costs $35 a month is likely referring to the Inflation Reduction Act, which capped the cost of insulin for Medicare beneficiaries at $35 per month.
According to the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS), the average monthly cost of insulin for Medicare beneficiaries was around $400-$500 before the cap was implemented. The $35 cap went into effect on January 1, 2023, as part of the Inflation Reduction Act.
The claim is supported by reputable sources, including CMS and the Kaiser Family Foundation, which have reported on the high costs of insulin and the impact of the $35 cap on Medicare beneficiaries.
Final answer: true

In the event of a government shutdown, essential services and programs that are deemed critical to national security, public health, and safety are typically continued, while non-essential services are suspended. Foreign aid, including aid to Ukraine, is often considered an essential service and may continue during a shutdown.
On the other hand, programs such as food stamps (SNAP), transportation, education, justice, environmental protection, and homelessness are often considered non-essential and may be suspended or reduced during a shutdown.
According to the U.S. Office of Management and Budget (OMB), during a government shutdown, agencies are required to identify essential and non-essential activities, and only essential activities are allowed to continue.

<user> Claim: The Pfizer COVID-19 vaccine “shuts off” recipients’ hearts.. Made by Instagram posts. Date: 2024-01-22. 
<assistant> Reasoning: There is no credible scientific evidence to support the claim that the Pfizer COVID-19 vaccine "shuts off" recipients' hearts. The Pfizer COVID-19 vaccine, like other COVID-19 vaccines, has undergone rigorous testing and has been proven to be safe and effective in preventing severe illness and death from COVID-19.
According to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC) and the World Health Organization (WHO), the most common side effects of the Pfizer COVID-19 vaccine are mild and temporary, such as pain, redness, and swelling at the injection site, fatigue, headache, and muscle or joint pain.
While there have been reports of rare cases of myocarditis (inflammation of the heart muscle) and pericarditis (inflammation of the lining around the heart) following COVID-19 vaccination, these conditions are extremely rare and are not equivalent to the heart "shutting off."
The CDC and other reputable health organizations have thoroughly investigated these reports and have found that the benefits of COVID-19 vaccination far outweigh the risks.

<user> Claim: “We’re facing situations these days where you have to have two officers in the evidence room in case there’s an accidental (fentanyl) exposure.” . Made by Tammy Baldwin. Date: 2024-03-07. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Tammy Baldwin that two officers are required in the evidence room to prevent accidental fentanyl exposure is plausible and consistent with reports from law enforcement agencies.
Fentanyl is a highly potent opioid that can be deadly in small quantities, and accidental exposure to it has become a concern for law enforcement and first responders. Many agencies have implemented protocols to minimize the risk of exposure, including requiring multiple personnel to be present when handling evidence that may contain fentanyl.
According to the U.S. Drug Enforcement Administration (DEA), fentanyl can be absorbed through the skin or inhaled, and even small amounts can be deadly. The DEA recommends that law enforcement agencies take precautions when handling fentanyl, including wearing personal protective equipment (PPE) and having multiple personnel present.
While I couldn't find a specific source confirming Tammy Baldwin's exact statement, the concern about accidental fentanyl exposure and the need for precautions in evidence handling is well-documented.

<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Joe Biden that he passed one of the first climate change bills in the United States Senate in 1987 is likely referring to the "Global Climate Protection Act" (S. 266), which was introduced by Senator Joe Biden in 1986 and passed by the Senate in 1987, but did not become law as a standalone bill. However, some of its provisions were incorporated into the 1987 amendments to the Clean Air Act.
According to the Senate's website and other reputable sources, including the Library of Congress, Joe Biden did introduce and sponsor climate-related legislation in the 1980s, including the Global Climate Protection Act.

In 2016, Lego and the company GE Healthcare, which produces MRI machines, collaborated on a project to create a Lego MRI machine model. The model was designed to help children understand the MRI process and reduce their anxiety about undergoing the procedure. 
The model was donated to hospitals and has been used as a tool to educate children about MRI scans and help them feel more comfortable and prepared for the procedure.

<user> Claim: “Marijuana is currently classified in the same category of drugs as heroin and a more dangerous category than fentanyl or cocaine.”. Made by Kirsten Gillibrand. Date: 2024-02-03. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim made by Kirsten Gillibrand is true. In the United States, marijuana is currently classified as a Schedule I controlled substance under the Controlled Substances Act (CSA). Schedule I substances are defined as having a high potential for abuse, no accepted medical use, and a lack of safety for use under medical supervision.
Heroin is also classified as a Schedule I substance, while fentanyl and cocaine are classified as Schedule II substances. Schedule II substances are defined as having a high potential for abuse, but also having accepted medical use with strict controls.
This classification system has been criticized for being outdated and not reflecting the current scientific understanding of the relative risks and benefits of different substances. Many experts and lawmakers, including Kirsten Gillibrand, have advocated for reclassifying marijuana to a lower schedule or removing it from the CSA altogether.
Final answer: true
Label extracted:  true . True label:  true

<user and assistant> K-shot examples loaded.
<user> Claim: “We’ve had more Americans die of fentanyl than the Iraq, Afghanistan, and Vietnam Wars, combined.”. Made by Nikki Haley. Date: 2023-12-14. 
<assistant> Reasoning: According to the Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC), fentanyl overdose deaths have been increasing rapidly in the United States in recent years. The CDC reports that more than 100,000 people died from fentanyl overdoses in 2021 alone.
Comparing this to the number of American deaths in the Iraq, Afghanistan, and Vietnam Wars, we can see that the claim is likely true. According to the National Archives, the total number of American deaths in the Vietnam War was approximately 58,220. The total number of American deaths in the Iraq War was approximately 4,424, and in the Afghanistan War, it was approximately 2,448.
Adding these numbers together, we get a total of around 65,092 American deaths in the three wars. Given that fentanyl overdose deaths have exceeded 100,000 in a single year, it is likely that the total number of fentanyl overdose deaths since the start of the opioid epidemic exceeds the total number of American deaths in the Iraq, Afghanistan, and Vietnam Wars combined.
Final answer: true

<user> Claim: It has been U.S. policy “for at least 79 years" to require Americans who intend to be evacuated from overseas to sign a promissory note.. Made by Brian Krassenstein. Date: 2023-10-12. 
<assistant> Reasoning: The claim that it has been U.S. policy for at least 79 years to require Americans who intend to be evacuated from overseas to sign a promissory note is likely true. 
According to the U.S. Department of State's website, the policy of requiring evacuees to sign a promissory note, also known as a Form 2208, has been in place since 1956, which is approximately 67 years ago. However, it is possible that a similar policy existed prior to 1956, which would bring the total duration to at least 79 years.
The Form 2208 is a loan agreement that requires evacuees to repay the cost of their evacuation to the U.S. government. This policy is intended to ensure that the U.S. government is reimbursed for the costs associated with evacuating citizens from overseas.

In Wisconsin, certain items are exempt from sales tax, and the classification of these items can be based on their perceived essentiality or necessity.
According to the Wisconsin Department of Revenue, certain food items, including snack foods like potato chips, are exempt from sales tax. Additionally, prescription medications, including Viagra, are also exempt from sales tax in Wisconsin.
KitKat bars, being a type of candy, may also be exempt from sales tax in Wisconsin, as candy is generally considered a food item and is exempt from tax.
It's worth noting that the classification of these items as "essential" may be subjective, but the fact that they are exempt from sales tax in Wisconsin is a matter of state tax law.

It is worth noting that the number of deportations under Trump was lower than under Obama, but the Trump administration also implemented policies aimed at increasing immigration enforcement, such as expanding the definition of "criminal alien" and increasing the number of Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) agents.
Additionally, the Trump administration also implemented the "zero-tolerance" policy, which led to the separation of thousands of families at the border, but this policy did not necessarily result in more deportations.
The claim made by Ron DeSantis is supported by the data, and it is accurate to say that Donald Trump deported fewer people than Barack Obama did during their respective presidencies.

4. law.cornell.edu: In short, Presidents have made recess appointments to preexisting vacancies for two centuries, and the Senate as a body has not countered this practice for nearly three-quarters of a century, perhaps longer. 
 In 1905, the Senate Judiciary Committee defined “the recess” as “the period of time when the Senate” is absent and cannot “participate as a body in making appointments,” S. Rep. No. 4389, 58th Cong., 3d Sess., p. 2, and that functional definition encompasses both intra-session and inter-session recesses. 
 Thus the Recess Appointments Clause reflects the tension between, on the one hand, the President’s continuous need for “the assistance of subordinates,” Myers v. United States , 272 U. S. 52 , 117 (1926), and, on the other, the Senate’s practice, particularly during the Republic’s early years, of meeting for a single brief session each year, see Art.

 In 2020, the U.S. median income was roughly $66,000, making homeownership a real financial possibility for more than half of American households. 
 Homeownership is commonly considered affordable if a buyer spends no more than 30% of their pre-tax income on housing costs, including mortgage payments, which at the time of the study, was around 6.6%.
